## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Platform Engineering: CODEOWNERS Infrastructure Discovery

## Your Task

Your platform team needs to understand how code ownership works in Grafana — not just the CODEOWNERS file itself, but the entire infrastructure around it: manifest generation, CI validation, Go integration with feature management, and npm scripts.

**Specific question**: Find all files in `grafana/grafana` that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure:

1. **The actual CODEOWNERS file** — the GitHub ownership definition
2. **CI workflows** that validate CODEOWNERS
3. **Manifest generation scripts** (JavaScript) that parse and index CODEOWNERS
4. **Go code** that defines the `codeowner` type for feature management
5. **npm scripts** that orchestrate manifest generation

This crosses YAML (CI), JavaScript (scripts), Go (backend), and file ownership conventions.

## Context

You are a platform engineer investigating how code ownership is implemented and enforced in a large monorepo. Understanding this infrastructure is critical for onboarding new teams, debugging CI failures related to CODEOWNERS validation, and extending the ownership system to new areas of the codebase.

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "grafana/grafana", "path": "relative/path/to/file"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of the CODEOWNERS infrastructure."
}
```

**Important**: Use `"grafana/grafana"` for the repo name. Strip `github.com/` prefix.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/grafana/grafana`). Strip this prefix in your answer.

Include only the `files` field. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all files that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure?
- **Keyword presence**: Does your answer reference key identifiers (CODEOWNERS, codeowners-manifest, codeowner)?

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with **21 files** that form the complete CODEOWNERS infrastructure:

### Core Files:
- **`.github/CODEOWNERS`** - The actual CODEOWNERS file with GitHub team/user ownership mappings

- **`pkg/services/featuremgmt/codeowners.go`** - Defines the `codeowner` type and constants for all teams

- **`pkg/services/featuremgmt/toggles_gen_test.go`** - Test file that generates all manifests when run
- **`Makefile`** - `gen-feature-toggles` target that orchestrates generation
- **`package.json`** - `betterer:issues` npm script for manifest generation

### Generated Manifests:
- **`toggles_gen.json`** - Kubernetes-style feature list
- **`toggles_gen.csv`** - CSV export of features with ownership
- **`featureToggles.gen.ts`** - TypeScript type definitions
- **`toggles_gen.go`** - Generated Go constants
- **`feature-toggles/index.md`** - Generated documentation

### CODEOWNERS Parsing:
- **`scripts/cli/generateBettererIssues.ts`** - TypeScript script that parses CODEOWNERS using the `codeowners` npm package to assign issues to team owners

### Supporting Files:
- Kubernetes API types, OpenAPI schema, and registration
- Configuration and documentation files

across the repository, tightly integrated with feature management.\\n\\nAt its core is the `.github/CODEOWNERS` file, which is the standard GitHub ownership definition used for pull request routing and review assignment. This file maps file patterns to GitHub teams and individuals using the format documented by GitHub.\\n\\nThe CODEOWNERS file is validated by a CI workflow (`.github/workflows/codeowners-validator.yml`) that runs on every pull request. It uses the mszostok/codeowners-validator GitHub Action to check for syntax errors, duplicate patterns, and coverage issues.\\n\\nThe platform integrates CODEOWNERS with Grafana's feature management system. The `codeowner` type (defined in `pkg/services/featuremgmt/codeowners.go`) is a string type representing GitHub team or user references. This type is used in the `FeatureFlag` struct (`pkg/services/featuremgmt/models.go`) to assign ownership of each feature toggle to a specific team.\\n\\nFeature flags are registered in `pkg/services/featuremgmt/registry.go` with metadata including the `Owner` field. The manifest generation process is orchestrated by `pkg/services/featuremgmt/toggles_gen_test.go`, which is a test file that generates multiple artifacts when executed: a Kubernetes-style feature list (`toggles_gen.json`), a CSV export (`toggles_gen.csv`), TypeScript type definitions (`featureToggles.gen.ts`), Go constants (`toggles_gen.go`), and Markdown documentation.\\n\\nGeneration is triggered via `make gen-feature-toggles` (defined in the `Makefile`) or by running the Go tests directly. The process can also be invoked through npm scripts, specifically `betterer:issues` which uses the TypeScript script `scripts/cli/generateBettererIssues.ts`.\\n\\nThe `generateBettererIssues.ts` script demonstrates how the CODEOWNERS infrastructure is consumed by other tools. It imports and uses the `codeowners` npm package (version ^5.1.1 from `package.json`) to parse the CODEOWNERS file and assign code quality issues to the appropriate team owners.\\n\\nThe Kubernetes API layer provides structured types for features (`pkg/apis/featuretoggle/v0alpha1/types.go`) and auto-generated OpenAPI schema (`zz_generated.openapi.go`), enabling feature toggles to be managed as first-class Kubernetes resources with the `codeowner` field.\\n\\nThis infrastructure ensures that code ownership is centralized, validated, and can be automatically distributed to systems that need to route work (like issue assignment, code review, or quality analysis) based on team ownership.\"\n}\n",
